<Time>1611534693969<//Time>< review>
I hiked this in snow. It was incredibly beautiful. It would take a poet to do the view at the top justice.

Be VERY careful when there's ice. Things get very slippery, especially near the summit. It would be very easy to slip and careen off the side to your death, so hold fast to the handrails near the top and take it slowly and surely.

There's no signal on T-Mobile for most of the hike, but the summit had signal, in case you need to make an emergency call.</review>

<rating>5</rating><Review>We arrived at 830 am.  You must park across the street and pay $10 for parking.  The trail is absolutely beautiful and there was plenty of shade as the brush is very tall on both sides.  It's 2 miles to the top, and fairly easy trail.  We saw 2 snakes but both were getting out of our way. The view at the top is amazing, overlooking miles and miles all the way around.  The top is the best part, be sure to climb up the steps to the top.  We had a snack, took pictures and headed down the hill.  It's an easy walk down.  I love this hike it was fast and easy for us. I was back in San Diego at noon.<//Review>< Pictures>

<Review>ŸÖŸÜ ŸÑÿß ŸäÿÆÿßŸÅ ÿßŸÑŸÑŸáÿå ŸÑÿß ŸäÿÆÿßŸÅ ÿßŸÑŸÑŸá ŸÅŸä ÿÆŸÑŸÇŸá. Ÿà Ÿäÿß ÿ£ÿπÿ∏ŸÖ ÿßŸÑŸÑŸá ŸàŸäÿß ÿπÿ∏ŸäŸÖ ÿÆŸÑŸÇŸá. This place serves as a reminder that the world is not ours alone and that no matter how mighty man thinks himself, if he's left to breach rights, he will eventually face consequences. That is all I will say. üåäüêß#sticksandstones #breakyourbones
__________________________

It was 2017, about 9 months after I left my job but missed the scholarship application by a mere hour. I stayed for 3 months in an economics program I could bearly afford but what I truly wanted was the Masters in Art Management given in partnership with Sotheby's. My mom was inconclusively sick at the time and our house was in practical shambles. We were a happy family until sorrow started hacking at my brother and trickling its way through to all of us. I decided it was time to come back home even if empty and without much hope. As a last resort, I passed by here to get turquoise aka fayrouz, the stone not the artist, which Islamically is touted for its ability to ward off evil eyes. I walk in and the owner and his family were sat down beside their scruffy dog. At first I think they're glaring because I'm a hijabi. Then after a while he comes to me, the owner, and says out of the blue: "We all go to heaven when we die, right?" And thankfully he went from that awkward opening as I stood there a bit confused to asking about what I gravitated towards. He then left me to look around and I'd found my way through the sliding doors to the outdoor corridor. I'm not sure if it was the painting which depicted burning men alive during the plague or the wooden shed at the end but something made me feel so uneasy that I froze and stared at the display case by the sliding doors for a good 5 minutes until my dad came in yelling from the parking lot. Not to enforce stereotypes but yes he's your typical Ed, *cough* Abdullah *cough* Ed. My mom passed away 7 months later. No, I wasn't wearing black that day. I still have no idea why anyone would open with a question about death.</Review><Pictures>None<//Pictures><Resp>None<//Resp>< gmap_id>
